###begin article-title 0
###xml 40 62 40 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neorickettsia risticii</italic>
###xml 40 62 <span type="species:ncbi:950">Neorickettsia risticii</span>
###xml 91 96 <span type="species:ncbi:9796">horse</span>
Analysis of complete genome sequence of Neorickettsia risticii: causative agent of Potomac horse fever
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 0 22 0 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neorickettsia risticii</italic>
###xml 187 198 187 198 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 252 263 252 263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 382 393 382 393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 593 604 593 604 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. sennetsu</italic>
###xml 675 686 675 686 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 691 702 691 702 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. sennetsu</italic>
###xml 739 740 739 740 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N</italic>
###xml 742 750 742 750 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">risticii</italic>
###xml 1040 1051 1040 1051 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 1395 1406 1395 1406 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 0 22 <span type="species:ncbi:950">Neorickettsia risticii</span>
###xml 93 99 <span type="species:ncbi:9796">Horses</span>
###xml 116 121 <span type="species:ncbi:9796">horse</span>
###xml 187 198 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 252 263 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 382 393 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 578 583 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 593 604 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 675 686 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 691 702 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 739 750 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 1040 1051 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 1395 1406 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
Neorickettsia risticii is an obligate intracellular bacterium of the trematodes and mammals. Horses develop Potomac horse fever (PHF) when they ingest aquatic insects containing encysted N. risticii-infected trematodes. The complete genome sequence of N. risticii Illinois consists of a single circular chromosome of 879 977 bp and encodes 38 RNA species and 898 proteins. Although N. risticii has limited ability to synthesize amino acids and lacks many metabolic pathways, it is capable of making major vitamins, cofactors and nucleotides. Comparison with its closely related human pathogen N. sennetsu showed that 758 (88.2%) of protein-coding genes are conserved between N. risticii and N. sennetsu. Four-way comparison of genes among N. risticii and other Anaplasmataceae showed that most genes are either shared among Anaplasmataceae (525 orthologs that generally associated with housekeeping functions), or specific to each genome (>200 genes that are mostly hypothetical proteins). Genes potentially involved in the pathogenesis of N. risticii were identified, including those encoding putative outer membrane proteins, two-component systems and a type IV secretion system (T4SS). The bipolar localization of T4SS pilus protein VirB2 on the bacterial surface was demonstrated for the first time in obligate intracellular bacteria. These data provide insights toward genomic potential of N. risticii and intracellular parasitism, and facilitate our understanding of PHF pathogenesis.
###end p 1
###begin title 2
INTRODUCTION
###end title 2
###begin p 3
###xml 265 266 265 266 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 267 268 267 268 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B2">2</xref>
###xml 402 403 402 403 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>
###xml 508 530 508 530 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neorickettsia sennetsu</italic>
###xml 626 627 626 627 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B2">2</xref>
###xml 628 629 628 629 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B4">4</xref>
###xml 669 691 669 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neorickettsia risticii</italic>
###xml 702 720 702 720 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ehrlichia risticii</italic>
###xml 723 734 723 734 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 815 816 815 816 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 817 818 817 818 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B5">5</xref>
###xml 957 958 957 958 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 959 960 959 960 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7">7</xref>
###xml 111 116 <span type="species:ncbi:9796">horse</span>
###xml 184 190 <span type="species:ncbi:9796">horses</span>
###xml 508 530 <span type="species:ncbi:951">Neorickettsia sennetsu</span>
###xml 545 550 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 603 609 <span type="species:ncbi:9796">horses</span>
###xml 669 691 <span type="species:ncbi:950">Neorickettsia risticii</span>
###xml 702 720 <span type="species:ncbi:950">Ehrlichia risticii</span>
###xml 723 734 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
Characterized by fever, depression, anorexia, dehydration, watery diarrhea, laminitis and/or abortion, Potomac horse fever (PHF) is an acute, often severe to fatal systemic disease of horses and typically occurs in the warm weather months of middle to late summer (1,2). The outbreak of PHF in the 1970s along the Potomac River in Maryland and Virginia helped to recognize PHF as a new disease entity (3). Subsequent investigations led to the ultrastructural observation of intracellular bacteria similar to Neorickettsia sennetsu, the agent of human Sennetsu neorickettsiosis, in intestinal tissues of horses with acute PHF (2,4) and the discovery of a new bacterium, Neorickettsia risticii (formerly Ehrlichia risticii). N. risticii was demonstrated as the causative agent of PHF by fulfilling Koch's postulates (1,5). Currently, PHF is frequently found throughout North America and increasingly recognized in South America, including Brazil and Uruguay (6,7).
###end p 3
###begin p 4
###xml 28 41 28 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neorickettsia</italic>
###xml 241 252 241 252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 407 408 407 408 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 434 447 434 447 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neorickettsia</italic>
###xml 666 667 666 667 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 700 711 700 711 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 795 818 795 818 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Acanthatrium oregonense</italic>
###xml 906 922 906 922 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Elimia virginica</italic>
###xml 1080 1081 1080 1081 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 1082 1086 1082 1086 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8 B9 B10 B11">8&#8211;11</xref>
###xml 1107 1118 1107 1118 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 1194 1205 1194 1205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 1378 1379 1378 1379 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B2">2</xref>
###xml 1380 1385 1380 1385 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11 B12 B13">11&#8211;13</xref>
###xml 1536 1538 1536 1538 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 1744 1755 1744 1755 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 1778 1780 1778 1780 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 1781 1783 1781 1783 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 241 252 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 700 711 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 906 922 <span type="species:ncbi:101406">Elimia virginica</span>
###xml 1107 1118 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 1186 1192 <span type="species:ncbi:9796">horses</span>
###xml 1194 1205 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 1257 1263 <span type="species:ncbi:9796">horses</span>
###xml 1744 1755 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
In the natural environment, Neorickettsia spp. reside inside trematodes, which can be transstadially transmitted through all developmental stages of trematodes and transovarially passed through generations of trematodes. The relationship of N. risticii with its trematode host seems to be either commensal or mutualistic, as reproduction of trematodes does not appear to be adversely affected by infection (8). Mammalian infection by Neorickettsia spp. occurs by horizontal transmission of the bacterium from trematodes to susceptible mammalian hosts, mostly through ingestion of this bacterium in the metacercarial stage of trematodes encysting in insects or fish (6). In the eastern United States, N. risticii is maintained by transstadial and transovarial passage in the digenetic trematode, Acanthatrium oregonense, which has a complex life cycle consisting of miracidia and sporocysts in snail hosts (Elimia virginica), free-swimming cercariae, metacercariae in aquatic insects (caddisflies, mayflies), and adults that lay eggs in the intestinal lumen of insectivorous bats (6,8-11). Upon ingestion of N. risticii in the metacercarial stage of the trematodes in aquatic insects by horses, N. risticii is horizontally transmitted from the trematodes to horses and replicates within inclusion bodies inside monocytes, macrophages, mast cells and intestinal epithelial cells (2,11-13). Currently, the only effective treatment of PHF is the administration of broad-spectrum tetracycline antibiotics in the early stages of the disease (11). Although a vaccine against PHF has been marketed, PHF continues to cause widespread infections, probably due to both the insufficient immunity developed by the vaccination and the antigenic variation of N. risticii strains in the field (14,15).
###end p 4

###xml 2263 2264 2263 2264 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</sup>
###xml 2294 2303 2294 2303 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Anaplasma</italic>
###xml 2308 2317 2308 2317 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ehrlichia</italic>
###xml 2263 2416 2263 2416 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="7"><sup>a</sup>Transmission mode: Except for <italic>Anaplasma</italic> and <italic>Ehrlichia</italic> species, all these listed organisms can be transovarially transmitted (TOP, Transovarial passage).</p>
###xml 2263 2416 2263 2416 <fn xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="TF1"><p textid="7"><sup>a</sup>Transmission mode: Except for <italic>Anaplasma</italic> and <italic>Ehrlichia</italic> species, all these listed organisms can be transovarially transmitted (TOP, Transovarial passage).</p></fn>
###xml 2416 2417 2416 2417 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">b</sup>
###xml 2625 2634 2625 2634 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Wolbachia</italic>
###xml 2645 2652 2645 2652 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Science</italic>
###xml 2416 2670 2416 2670 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="8"><sup>b</sup>Filarial nematode causes debilitating inflammatory diseases such as river blindness and lymphatic filariasis. However, the predominant inflammatory response in the cornea is due to a species of endosymbiotic <italic>Wolbachia</italic> bacteria (<italic>Science</italic> 295: 1982, 2002).</p>
###xml 2416 2670 2416 2670 <fn xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="TF2"><p textid="8"><sup>b</sup>Filarial nematode causes debilitating inflammatory diseases such as river blindness and lymphatic filariasis. However, the predominant inflammatory response in the cornea is due to a species of endosymbiotic <italic>Wolbachia</italic> bacteria (<italic>Science</italic> 295: 1982, 2002).</p></fn>
###xml 2263 2670 2263 2670 <table-wrap-foot xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><fn id="TF1"><p textid="7"><sup>a</sup>Transmission mode: Except for <italic>Anaplasma</italic> and <italic>Ehrlichia</italic> species, all these listed organisms can be transovarially transmitted (TOP, Transovarial passage).</p></fn><fn id="TF2"><p textid="8"><sup>b</sup>Filarial nematode causes debilitating inflammatory diseases such as river blindness and lymphatic filariasis. However, the predominant inflammatory response in the cornea is due to a species of endosymbiotic <italic>Wolbachia</italic> bacteria (<italic>Science</italic> 295: 1982, 2002).</p></fn></table-wrap-foot>

###xml 139 150 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 152 163 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 174 192 <span type="species:ncbi:951">Ehrlichia sennetsu</span>
###xml 197 216 <span type="species:ncbi:951">Rickettsia sennetsu</span>
###xml 222 237 <span type="species:ncbi:33994">N. helminthoeca</span>
###xml 280 284 <span type="species:ncbi:9615">dogs</span>
###xml 467 488 <span type="species:ncbi:945">Ehrlichia chaffeensis</span>
###xml 490 515 <span type="species:ncbi:948">Anaplasma phagocytophilum</span>
###xml 524 563 <span type="species:ncbi:80849">Wolbachia endosymbiont of Brugia malayi</span>
###xml 588 599 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 690 701 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 986 997 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 1002 1013 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 1401 1406 <span type="species:ncbi:9796">horse</span>
###xml 1607 1629 <span type="species:ncbi:240278">Nanophyetus salmincola</span>
###xml 1779 1782 <span type="species:ncbi:9685">Cat</span>
###xml 1792 1797 <span type="species:ncbi:9940">Sheep</span>
###xml 1799 1805 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">Cattle</span>
###xml 1807 1812 <span type="species:ncbi:9796">Horse</span>
###xml 1814 1817 <span type="species:ncbi:9615">Dog</span>
###xml 1819 1828 <span type="species:ncbi:9823">Wild boar</span>
###xml 1849 1862 <span type="species:ncbi:6945">I. scapularis</span>
###xml 1864 1874 <span type="species:ncbi:34613">I. ricinus</span>
###xml 1876 1890 <span type="species:ncbi:34615">I. persulcatus</span>
###xml 2010 2030 <span type="species:ncbi:6943">Amblyomma americanum</span>
So far, Neorickettsia spp. that cause significant illness in mammals have been studied sufficiently to be officially classified. These are N. risticii, N. sennetsu (formerly Ehrlichia sennetsu and Rickettsia sennetsu) and N. helminthoeca, the agent of Salmon poisoning disease in dogs (Table 1) (6,16,17). The 16S rRNA-based phylogenic tree shows that Neorickettsia species reside in a clade separated from other Anaplasmataceae in the order Rickettsiales, including Ehrlichia chaffeensis, Anaplasma phagocytophilum and the Wolbachia endosymbiont of Brugia malayi (wBm) (Figure 1). While N. risticii infects a trematode that uses an aquatic insect as an intermediate host in North America, N. sennetsu infects a trematode that likely uses a fish as an intermediate host in Southeast Asia (6,11). Despite distinct trematode and mammalian hosts, pathogenesis and geographic ranges, phylogenetic analysis based on the 16S rRNA sequence indicates that there is only 0.7% divergence between N. risticii and N. sennetsu (Figure 1). ###begin p 10
###xml 26 37 26 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 138 149 138 149 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. sennetsu</italic>
###xml 184 197 184 197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neorickettsia</italic>
###xml 328 339 328 339 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 374 387 374 387 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neorickettsia</italic>
###xml 396 409 396 409 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neorickettsia</italic>
###xml 590 591 590 591 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 26 37 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 138 149 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 328 339 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
In the present study, the N. risticii genome is sequenced, compared with those of other members of the family Anaplasmataceae, especially N. sennetsu: the only sequenced member of the Neorickettsia genus with unknown trematode association, and potential virulence factors and novel outer membrane proteins are identified. While N. risticii is the newest member of the genus Neorickettsia, of all Neorickettsia spp., it has the broadest geographic distribution, inflicting the greatest economical and emotional loss, and the best information available for pathogenesis and immune responses (6). These genome sequence data will be critical for enhancing our knowledge of this obligate intracellular bacterium, providing tools for better understanding PHF pathogenesis, and the development of effective vaccines.
###end p 10
###begin title 11
MATERIALS AND METHODS
###end title 11
###begin title 12
###xml 28 39 28 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 28 39 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
Culture and purification of N. risticii genomic DNA
###end title 12
###begin p 13
###xml 0 22 0 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neorickettsia risticii</italic>
###xml 31 32 31 32 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">T</sup>
###xml 101 103 101 103 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 106 128 106 128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neorickettsia risticii</italic>
###xml 161 162 161 162 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 279 280 279 280 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">l</sc>
###xml 312 313 312 313 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 372 374 366 368 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 555 557 549 551 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 0 22 <span type="species:ncbi:950">Neorickettsia risticii</span>
###xml 106 137 <span type="species:ncbi:434131">Neorickettsia risticii Illinois</span>
###xml 172 178 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 257 263 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
Neorickettsia risticii IllinoisT was obtained from the Naval Medical Research Center (Bethesda, MD) (11). Neorickettsia risticii Illinois was propagated in P388D1 cells, a murine monocytic leukemia cell line, in RPMI 1640 medium supplemented with 10% fetal bovine serum and 2 mM l-glutamine in a humidified 5% CO2-95% air atmosphere at 37degreesC as previously described (18). Bacterial cells were liberated from the infected host cells using Dounce homogenization, and purified by differential centrifugation and Percoll density gradient centrifugation (17). Any specimens with host nuclei contamination were excluded. From these isolated bacteria, phenol extraction was used to purify DNA that was minimally fragmented and free of host-cell DNA. Levels of host DNA contamination were verified to be less than 0.01% by PCR using host G3PDH-specific primers.
###end p 13
###begin title 14
Genome sequencing, gap closure and assembly
###end title 14
###begin p 15
###xml 14 25 14 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 447 458 447 458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 501 512 501 512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. sennetsu</italic>
###xml 791 793 791 793 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 14 25 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 447 458 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 501 512 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
The genome of N. risticii Illinois was sequenced with shotgun sequencing at 20x coverage using a pyrosequencing protocol in a microfabricated high-density picoliter reaction (454 Life Sciences, Branford, CT). Eight major contigs (>16 kb each) and five minor contigs (629-5105 bp) were obtained, and gaps were closed by primer walking. All PCR primers were designed around 200 bp from the ends of each contigs, with the positions of contigs in the N. risticii genome predicted by blasting those to the N. sennetsu genome (GenBank No. NC_007798). The whole genome was assembled from the contigs and the sequenced gap segments by the SeqMan program from the Lasergene DNAStar software package (Madison, WI). The GC-skew was calculated as (C-G)/(C+G) in windows of 1000 bp along the chromosome (19).
###end p 15
###begin title 16
Genome annotation and comparison with other related organisms
###end title 16
###begin p 17
###xml 627 629 627 629 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 922 923 922 923 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 923 924 923 924 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</sub>
###xml 925 926 925 926 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 926 927 926 927 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 1128 1130 1128 1130 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
The DNA sequence was submitted to the JCVI (J. Craig Venter Institute) Annotation Service, where it was run through JCVI's prokaryotic annotation pipeline (). Included in the pipeline is gene finding with Glimmer 2, Blast-extend-repraze (BER) searches, HMM (a hidden Markov model) searches, TMHMM (transmembrane helix prediction) searches, SignalP predictions and automatic annotations from AutoAnnotate. Potential protein and RNA-coding sequences were predicted and annotated from these tools, including feature identification (e.g. protein motifs), and assignment of database matches and functional role categories to genes (17). The manual annotation tool Manatee was downloaded from SourceForge () and used to manually review and curate the output from the prokaryotic pipeline of the JCVI Annotation Service. Ribosome binding sites (RBS) were determined by RBSFinder (ftp://ftp.tigr.org/pub/software/RBSfinder/). The Ka/Ks ratio was determined using WSPMaker with the sliding window method (), a web based tool to calculate and display the selection pressure in sub-regions of two orthologous protein-coding DNA sequences (20).
###end p 17
###begin p 18
###xml 167 178 167 178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 202 213 202 213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. sennetsu</italic>
###xml 215 229 215 229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. chaffeensis</italic>
###xml 231 249 231 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. phagocytophilum</italic>
###xml 254 263 254 263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Wolbachia</italic>
###xml 311 322 311 322 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 445 446 445 446 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 451 453 451 453 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8211;5</sup>
###xml 534 536 534 536 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 553 555 553 555 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 167 178 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 202 213 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 215 229 <span type="species:ncbi:945">E. chaffeensis</span>
###xml 231 249 <span type="species:ncbi:948">A. phagocytophilum</span>
###xml 311 322 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
Phylogenetic trees were constructed based on sequence alignment by the Clustal W method using the MegAlign program from the Lasergene package. Comparative analysis of N. risticii and related organisms (N. sennetsu, E. chaffeensis, A. phagocytophilum and Wolbachia wBm) was performed by using reciprocal BLASTP. N. risticii genes with or without homology to other related organisms were identified by reciprocal BLASTP hits with cutoff scores of E < 10-5. Signal peptides and transmembrane helices were predicted by using SignalP 3.0 (21) and TMHMM 2.0 (22) set at default values.
###end p 18
###begin title 19
###xml 32 43 32 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 58 59 58 59 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 32 43 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
Analysis of VirB2 expression in N. risticii-infected P388D1 cells
###end title 19
###begin p 20
###xml 29 34 29 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">virB2</italic>
###xml 38 49 38 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 80 91 80 91 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 106 107 106 107 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 205 212 205 212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">virB2.1</italic>
###xml 217 224 217 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">virB2.2</italic>
###xml 259 261 259 261 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 360 362 360 362 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 427 432 427 432 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32&#8211;46</sup>
###xml 454 465 454 465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 38 49 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 80 91 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 385 391 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 454 465 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
To detect gene expression of virB2 in N. risticii, total RNA was extracted from N. risticii-infected P388D1 cells at 3 days post-infection (p.i.) and RT-PCR was carried out using specific primers spanning virB2.1 and virB2.2 genes () as described previously (23). The expression of VirB2 protein was confirmed by western blot analysis as described previously (23), using custom-raised rabbit antisera against 15-mer peptide (aa32-46: AGPDKDDSIVSRVIC) of N. risticii VirB2-1 (NRI_0738) (Sigma-Genosys, Woodlands, TX).
###end p 20
###begin title 21
Double immunofluorescence labeling
###end title 21
###begin p 22
###xml 0 22 0 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neorickettsia risticii</italic>
###xml 37 38 37 38 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sub>
###xml 64 75 64 75 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 120 122 120 122 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 309 331 309 331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Neorickettsia risticii</italic>
###xml 424 435 424 435 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 546 557 546 557 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 580 591 580 591 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 0 22 <span type="species:ncbi:950">Neorickettsia risticii</span>
###xml 64 75 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 309 331 <span type="species:ncbi:950">Neorickettsia risticii</span>
###xml 424 435 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 535 540 <span type="species:ncbi:9796">horse</span>
###xml 546 557 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 568 574 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 580 591 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 667 673 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 781 785 <span type="species:ncbi:9925">goat</span>
###xml 791 796 <span type="species:ncbi:9796">horse</span>
###xml 869 873 <span type="species:ncbi:9925">goat</span>
###xml 879 885 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
Neorickettsia risticii-infected P388D1 cells at 2 days p.i., or N. risticii organisms purified as previously described (24), were centrifuged onto glass slides using a Shandon Cytospin 4 cytocentrifuge (Thermo Fisher Scientific, Kalamazoo, MI) and fixed in 4% paraformaldehyde at room temperature for 15 min. Neorickettsia risticii-infected cells were permeabilized with 0.1% saponin for 15 min and washed, whereas purified N. risticii organisms were subjected to labeling without saponin permeabilization. Samples were incubated with horse anti-N. risticii serum and rabbit anti-N. risticii VirB2 (NRI_0738) antibody in phosphate-buffered saline (PBS) containing 1% bovine serum albumin for 1 h at room temperature. After washing with PBS, cells were labeled with FITC-conjugated goat anti-horse (Jackson ImmunoResearch, West Grove, PA) and Alexa Fluor 555-conjugated goat anti-rabbit (Invitrogen, Carlsbad, CA) secondary antibodies for 1 h. Fluorescence images were analyzed and captured by a SPOT CCD digital camera (Diagnostic Instruments, Sterling Heights, MI) connected to a Nikon Eclipse E400 fluorescent microscope with a xenon-mercury light source (Nikon Instruments Inc, Melville, NY).
###end p 22

###end title 23

The sequence data described here have been deposited in GenBank (accession number CP001431).
###end p 24

###xml 1432 1441 1420 1429 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 2.</label>
###xml 1482 1493 1470 1481 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 2380 2391 2368 2379 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. sennetsu</italic>
###xml 1441 2591 1429 2579 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="31">Circular representation of the genome of <italic>N. risticii</italic>. From outside to inside, the first two circles represent predicted protein-coding sequences (ORFs) on the plus and minus strands, respectively. Colors indicate the role categories of ORFs: dark gray: hypothetical proteins or proteins with unknown functions; gold: amino-acid and protein biosynthesis; sky blue: purines, pyrimidines, nucleosides and nucleotides; cyan: fatty acid and phospholipid metabolism; light blue: biosynthesis of cofactors, prosthetic groups and carriers; aquamarine: central intermediary metabolism; royal blue: energy metabolism; pink: transport and binding proteins; dark orange: DNA metabolism and transcription; pale green: protein fate; tomato: regulatory functions and signal transduction; peach puff: cell envelope; pink: cellular processes; maroon: mobile and extrachromosomal element functions. The third and fourth circles show unique ORFs compared to <italic>N. sennetsu</italic>. The fifth and sixth circles represent RNA genes, including tRNAs (blue), rRNAs (orange), and sRNAs (red). The seventh circle represents G&#8211;C skew values [(G &#8211; C)/(G + C)] with a windows size of 1 kb.</p>
###xml 1441 2591 1429 2579 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><p textid="31">Circular representation of the genome of <italic>N. risticii</italic>. From outside to inside, the first two circles represent predicted protein-coding sequences (ORFs) on the plus and minus strands, respectively. Colors indicate the role categories of ORFs: dark gray: hypothetical proteins or proteins with unknown functions; gold: amino-acid and protein biosynthesis; sky blue: purines, pyrimidines, nucleosides and nucleotides; cyan: fatty acid and phospholipid metabolism; light blue: biosynthesis of cofactors, prosthetic groups and carriers; aquamarine: central intermediary metabolism; royal blue: energy metabolism; pink: transport and binding proteins; dark orange: DNA metabolism and transcription; pale green: protein fate; tomato: regulatory functions and signal transduction; peach puff: cell envelope; pink: cellular processes; maroon: mobile and extrachromosomal element functions. The third and fourth circles show unique ORFs compared to <italic>N. sennetsu</italic>. The fifth and sixth circles represent RNA genes, including tRNAs (blue), rRNAs (orange), and sRNAs (red). The seventh circle represents G&#8211;C skew values [(G &#8211; C)/(G + C)] with a windows size of 1 kb.</p></caption>

###xml 2622 2633 2610 2621 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 2665 2676 2653 2664 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. sennetsu</italic>
###xml 2687 2705 2675 2693 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. phagocytophilum</italic>

###xml 1321 1360 <span type="species:ncbi:80849">Wolbachia endosymbiont of Brugia malayi</span>
###xml 1482 1493 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 2160 2166 <span type="species:ncbi:4081">tomato</span>
###xml 2214 2219 <span type="species:ncbi:3760">peach</span>
###xml 2380 2391 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 2622 2633 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 2665 2676 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 2687 2708 <span type="species:ncbi:212042">A. phagocytophilum HZ</span>
###xml 2710 2733 <span type="species:ncbi:205920">E. chaffeensis Arkansas</span>
###xml 2743 2782 <span type="species:ncbi:80849">Wolbachia endosymbiont of Brugia malayi</span>
The genome of N. risticii consists of a single circular chromosome spanning 879 977 nt and has a G+C content of 41.3% (Table 2). The replication origin of the N. risticii was predicted based on one of the GC-skew shift points and the location of parB (Figure 2). This putative origin coincides with those of closely related species E. chaffeensis and N. sennetsu (17). The N. risticii and N. sennetsu genomes are smaller than those of other members in the family Anaplasmataceae, which are approximately1.0-1.5 Mb. In agreement with small 16S rRNA gene sequence divergence between N. risticii and N. sennetsu (Figure 1), the synteny plot between N. risticii and N. sennetsu indicates that these two genomes exhibit almost complete synteny, whereas no significant synteny is present with other members of the Anaplasmataceae (Figure 3). ###begin p 33
###xml 4 15 4 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 161 163 161 163 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 242 245 230 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sdh</italic>
###xml 255 273 243 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. phagocytophilum</italic>
###xml 275 277 263 265 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B25">25</xref>
###xml 367 378 355 366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 459 470 447 458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. sennetsu</italic>
###xml 472 479 460 467 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 769 776 757 764 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 781 789 769 777 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 4 15 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 255 273 <span type="species:ncbi:948">A. phagocytophilum</span>
###xml 367 378 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 459 470 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
The N. risticii genome encodes one copy of 5S, 16S and 23S rRNA genes. Similar to the other Anaplasmataceae sequenced, the 5S and 23S rRNA genes form an operon (17), while the 16S rRNA gene is separated by approximately0.7 Mb and followed by sdhCD, as in A. phagocytophilum (25). Thirty-three tRNA genes are identified, which include cognates for all 20 amino acids. N. risticii has a smaller number of predicted genes and a lower coding density (86.8%) than N. sennetsu (Table 2). Of 898 predicted protein-coding open reading frames (ORFs), 554 genes are assigned with probable functions based on similarity searches. Nearly 40% of the predicted ORFs (345 genes) in the genome are annotated as 'hypothetical' genes, either with conserved domains or unknown functions (Table 2 and Figure 2, gray bars in first two circles).
###end p 33
###begin p 34
###xml 16 27 16 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 329 333 329 333 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dnaB</italic>
###xml 641 643 641 643 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B26">26</xref>
###xml 644 646 644 646 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B27">27</xref>
###xml 698 709 698 709 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 16 27 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 698 709 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
Analysis of the N. risticii genome identified thirteen pairs of overlaps in protein-coding ORFs, and seven pairs of overlaps in RNA- and protein-coding genes (). Although most of the protein-coding ORFs that overlap with RNA genes encode small proteins (<50 aa) without any known functions, one encodes replicative DNA helicase (dnaB, NRI_0529), which potentially has essential functions for bacterial replication, and overlaps with an essential tRNA gene that decodes Proline (). Overlapping genes are detected primarily in parasitic or symbiotic bacteria and are believed to be a consequence of the reduction of originally larger genomes (26,27). Whether these overlapping genes are expressed by N. risticii remains to be experimentally verified.
###end p 34
###begin p 35
###xml 4 15 4 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 371 373 371 373 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B28">28</xref>
###xml 531 532 531 532 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</sub>

###xml 604 606 604 606 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>

###xml 614 615 614 615 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</sub>
###xml 616 617 616 617 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 617 618 617 618 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 677 678 677 678 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 678 679 678 679 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</sub>
###xml 718 719 718 719 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 719 720 719 720 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 812 814 812 814 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 983 994 983 994 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 999 1010 999 1010 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. sennetsu</italic>
###xml 1155 1156 1155 1156 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 1156 1157 1156 1157 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</sub>
###xml 1158 1159 1158 1159 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 1159 1160 1159 1160 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 1215 1226 1215 1226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 1231 1242 1231 1242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. sennetsu</italic>
###xml 1287 1298 1287 1298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 1328 1329 1328 1329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 1329 1330 1329 1330 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</sub>
###xml 1331 1332 1331 1332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 1332 1333 1332 1333 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 4 15 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 983 994 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 999 1010 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 1215 1226 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 1231 1242 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 1287 1298 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
The N. risticii genome has 110 ORFs that encode small hypothetical proteins with fewer than 60 amino acids. By RBSFinder analysis, 43 out of 110 (39%) do not have RBS upstream of the start codon. It is possible that translation of these leaderless mRNAs can be initiated via a novel pathway that involves the preassembled 70S ribosome rather than via a free 30S subunit (28). To determine whether these small protein-coding ORFs have evolved as typical coding genes with purifying selection restricting nonsynonymous changes, the Ka/Ks ratio was determined using WSPMaker with the sliding window method (20). The Ka/Ks ratio represents the rate of nonsynonymous substitutions (Ka) to that of synonymous substitutions (Ks), which can be used as an indicator of selective pressure acting on a protein-coding gene (29). Since WSPMaker takes orthologous protein-coding sequence pairs as input, we first used BLASTP to determine the small hypothetical proteins that are conserved between N. risticii and N. sennetsu. The resulting 26 orthologous ORF pairs were then concatenated with the stop codons removed (). Results demonstrated that, although the average Ka/Ks ratio of the concatenated 26 orthologous ORF pairs of N. risticii and N. sennetsu is 0.71, four regions, corresponding to six N. risticii protein-coding ORFs, exhibit Ka/Ks value >1 (). It suggests that these ORFs may have positive selection for advantageous mutations.
###end p 35
###begin p 36
###xml 113 115 113 115 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
###xml 116 118 116 118 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 186 197 186 197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 333 351 333 351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. phagocytophilum</italic>
###xml 479 481 467 469 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 530 544 518 532 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. chaffeensis</italic>
###xml 716 718 704 706 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B33">33</xref>
###xml 753 764 741 752 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 813 827 801 815 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. chaffeensis</italic>
###xml 832 850 820 838 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A. phagocytophilum</italic>
###xml 186 197 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 333 351 <span type="species:ncbi:948">A. phagocytophilum</span>
###xml 530 544 <span type="species:ncbi:945">E. chaffeensis</span>
###xml 753 764 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 813 827 <span type="species:ncbi:945">E. chaffeensis</span>
###xml 832 850 <span type="species:ncbi:948">A. phagocytophilum</span>
It has been suggested that around 10-30% of small protein-coding ORFs (<300 bp) do not actually encode proteins (30,31). As an obligate intracellular bacterium with a genome of <900 kb, N. risticii may share genomic features with closely related members in the family Anaplasmataceae. A whole genome transcription profiling study of A. phagocytophilum showed that approximately70% of ORFs were significantly transcribed, including 342 out of 409 ORFs (84%) of fewer than 180 bp (32). Furthermore, the global proteomic analysis of E. chaffeensis showed that more than 90% of 1115 predicted proteins were expressed, including 130 (62%) out of 209 proteins of fewer than 60 aa, most of which are hypothetical proteins (33). These data suggest that most of N. risticii small ORFs could also be transcribed similar to E. chaffeensis and A. phagocytophilum. As there is no definitive way to determine functional ORFs other than the experimental analysis, and all future analyses such as microarray and proteomics depend on the completeness of ORFs in curated genome sequences, we opt to retain all predicted ORFs in our annotation to facilitate future studies.
###end p 36

###xml 41 52 41 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
###xml 41 52 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>

###xml 42 53 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 109 120 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 122 136 <span type="species:ncbi:945">E. chaffeensis</span>
###xml 138 156 <span type="species:ncbi:948">A. phagocytophilum</span>
###xml 299 310 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 315 326 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 517 528 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 533 544 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 566 577 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 650 661 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 727 738 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 970 981 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 1088 1099 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 1281 1295 <span type="species:ncbi:42322|species:ncbi:779">E. ruminantium</span>
###xml 1297 1305 <span type="species:ncbi:944|species:ncbi:507819|species:ncbi:214095">E. canis</span>
###xml 1310 1322 <span type="species:ncbi:770">A. marginale</span>
###xml 1335 1340 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1359 1370 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 1372 1386 <span type="species:ncbi:945">E. chaffeensis</span>
###xml 1391 1409 <span type="species:ncbi:948">A. phagocytophilum</span>
###xml 1410 1415 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1634 1645 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 1862 1873 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 2148 2159 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 2724 2735 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 2818 2832 <span type="species:ncbi:945">E. chaffeensis</span>
###xml 2834 2852 <span type="species:ncbi:948">A. phagocytophilum</span>
###xml 2862 2901 <span type="species:ncbi:80849">Wolbachia endosymbiont of Brugia malayi</span>
###xml 2978 2989 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 2991 2994 <span type="species:ncbi:951">NSE</span>
In order to compare the genome content of N. risticii to representative members of Anaplasmataceae including N. sennetsu, E. chaffeensis, A. phagocytophilum and Wolbachia wBm, two-, three- and four-way comparisons were performed, and homologous clusters were constructed. Two-way comparison between N. risticii and N. sennetsu shows that these two genomes have 758 protein-coding ORFs that are orthologous to each other (88.2% of total protein-coding ORFs) (Figure 4A). Despite almost complete genome synteny between N. risticii and N. sennetsu, 140 (15.6% of total N. risticii ORFs, Figure 2, third and fourth circles) and 177 genes (18.9% of total N. sennetsu ORFs) are unique to each organism, respectively. Among them, 120 N. risticii genes (13.4%) do not exhibit similarity to any genes of either bacterial or eukaryotic origin (Table 3 and ). Functions of these predicted proteins are unknown, and their molecular masses range from 4.1 to 92.3 kDa. Of note, three N. risticii genes (0.3% of total genes) match only to genes in other Anaplasmataceae genomes, but not to genes in the N. sennetsu genome (). Two ORFs encoding Na+/H+ antiporter MnhB subunit-related proteins (NRI_0032/NRI_0033) are found only in members of Anaplasmataceae that primarily infect animals, such as E. ruminantium, E. canis and A. marginale, but not in human pathogens such as N. sennetsu, E. chaffeensis, or A. phagocytophilum human isolate. One conserved hypothetical protein matches to Wolbachia and Ehrlichia spp., with the characteristic C-terminal basic amino-acid motif for a type IV secretion system (T4SS) substrate (NRI_0703). Interestingly, N. risticii is the only sequenced species in the order Rickettsiales that encodes a complete DNA photolyase (deoxyribodipyrimidine photolyase, NRI_0805): an alternative mechanism for repairing UV-induced DNA damage (). Although N. sennetsu also encodes a DNA photolyase, it contains a point mutation at nt814 (CAA --> TAA), which results in a premature stop codon at aa271 (full-length protein length: approximately470 aa) and renders this ORF nonfunctional. ###xml 1884 2494 1880 2490 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><p textid="46">Comparison of the gene sets in members of the family Anaplasmataceae. ###xml 2494 2494 2490 2490 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkp642f4"/>
###xml 1875 2494 1871 2490 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F4" position="float"><label>Figure 4.</label><caption><p textid="46">Comparison of the gene sets in members of the family Anaplasmataceae. ###xml 35 46 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 100 111 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 382 393 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 734 748 <span type="species:ncbi:945">E. chaffeensis</span>
###xml 750 768 <span type="species:ncbi:948">A. phagocytophilum</span>
###xml 823 837 <span type="species:ncbi:945">E. chaffeensis</span>
###xml 842 860 <span type="species:ncbi:948">A. phagocytophilum</span>
###xml 902 913 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 1096 1107 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 1141 1155 <span type="species:ncbi:945">E. chaffeensis</span>
###xml 1160 1178 <span type="species:ncbi:948">A. phagocytophilum</span>
###xml 1591 1602 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 1607 1618 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 2342 2353 <span type="species:ncbi:951">N. sennetsu</span>
###xml 2355 2358 <span type="species:ncbi:951">NSE</span>
###xml 2361 2372 <span type="species:ncbi:950">N. risticii</span>
###xml 2383 2397 <span type="species:ncbi:945">E. chaffeensis</span>
###xml 2408 2426 <span type="species:ncbi:948">A. phagocytophilum</span>
###xml 2445 2484 <span type="species:ncbi:80849">Wolbachia endosymbiont of Brugia malayi</span>
Four-way comparison of genes among N. risticii and selected Anaplasmataceae members shows that most N. risticii genes are either shared among all Anaplasmataceae (525 orthologs) or specific to each genome (>200 ORFs) (Figure 4B). Analysis of these genes for functional categories indicates that most of the shared genes are associated with housekeeping functions (Table 3 and ). Of N. risticii-specific genes detected in this four-way comparison, the vast majority of these genes encode hypothetical, conserved hypothetical, and conserved domain proteins, as well as uncharacterized membrane proteins or lipoproteins (Table 3 and ). Two- and three-way comparisons show that most genes in these four genomes are either conserved among E. chaffeensis, A. phagocytophilum, and Wolbachia wBm (76 ortholog clusters), or between E. chaffeensis and A. phagocytophilum (53 ortholog clusters) (Figure 4B and ). N. risticii shares very limited numbers of ortholog clusters (mostly less than 10) in both two- and three-way comparisons (Figure 4B and ). The only exception is that, in three-way comparisons, N. risticii shares 38 ortholog clusters with E. chaffeensis and A. phagocytophilum, but not Wolbachia wBm (Figure 4B). Most of these orthologs are enzymes involved in vitamin and cofactor (biotin, folate and NAD) biosynthesis (15 orthologs, 40% of 38 orthologs), along with one putative transcriptional regulator (ECH_1118, APH_1218, or NRI_0223), suggesting a potential pathogenic trait or a niche adaption in mammalian hosts (). Interestingly, comparison with members of Anaplasmataceae shows N. risticii and N. sennetsu possess some genes that have either no homology or low homology to those in Anaplasmataceae, but higher homology to those of gamma-proteobacteria, such as HU DNA-binding proteins, ATP synthase subunits, DsbB/D protein, and some ribosomal protein subunits. Figure 4.Comparison of the gene sets in members of the family Anaplasmataceae. Venn diagram showing the comparison of conserved and unique genes between Neorickettsia spp. (A), or among selected members of the family Anaplasmataceae (B). Numbers within the intersections of different circles indicate ortholog clusters shared by 2, 3, or 4 organisms. (C) Comparison of gene sets by functional role category breakdown. Species indicated in the diagram are as follows: N. sennetsu (NSE), N. risticii (NRI, A), E. chaffeensis (ECH, C), A. phagocytophilum (APH, C), and the Wolbachia endosymbiont of Brugia malayi (WBM, D).
###end p 45

###begin p 47
###xml 18 29 18 29 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">N. risticii</italic>
